Eggeling
  1. Now Soma was in the sky, and the gods were here on earth. The gods desired,–‘Would that Soma came to us: we might sacrifice with him, when come.’ They created those two illusions, Suparс╣З─л and Kadr┼л. In the chapter on the hearths (dhishс╣Зya 1) it is set forth how that affair of Suparс╣З─л and Kadr┼л came to pass.

Eggeling
  1. The gods then created the lute and sat playing and singing, saying, ‘Thus we will sing to thee, thus we will amuse thee!’ She turned to the gods; but, in truth, she turned to them vainly, since she turned away from those, engaged in praising and praying, to dance and song. Wherefore even to this day women are given to vain things: for it was on this wise that V─Бc turned thereto, and other women do as she did. And hence it is to him who dances and sings that they most readily take a fancy 5.

Eggeling
  1. In the first place he pours the butter, which remains in the dhruv─Б spoon, in four parts into the guh┼л; and having tied a piece of gold with a blade of the altar-grass 8, and laid it down (in the juh┼л), he offers (the butter), thinking, ‘I will offer with pure milk;’ for milk and gold are of the same origin, since both have sprung from Agni’s seed 9.

Eggeling
  1. He lays down the piece of gold, with the text (V─Бj. S. IV, 17), ‘This (butter) is thy body, O shining (Agni)! this (gold) is thy light,’–for that gold is indeed light:–‘unite therewith and obtain splendour!’ When he says, ‘Unite therewith,’ he means to say, ‘Mingle therewith;’ and when he says, ‘Obtain splendour,’–splendour meaning Soma,–he means to say, ‘Obtain Soma.’

Eggeling
  1. And as the gods then sent her (V─Бc) to Soma, so does he now send her to Soma; and the cow for which the Soma is bought being in reality V─Бc, it is her he gratifies by this offering, thinking, ‘With her, when gratified, I shall buy the Soma.’

Eggeling
  1. He offers, with the text, ‘Thou art the singer of praises 12,’–for this (word ‘j┼лс╕е’), the ‘singer of praises,’ is one of her (V─Бc’s) names;–‘upholden by the Mind,’–this speech of ours

is indeed upheld by the mind, because the Mind goes before 13 Speech (and prompts her), ‘Speak thus! say not this!’ for, were it not for the Mind, Speech would indeed talk incoherently: for this reason he says, ‘Upholden by the Mind.’

Eggeling
  1. ‘Well-pleasing to Vishс╣Зu,’ whereby he means to say, ‘Well-pleasing to Soma whom we approach 14.’ [He proceeds, V─Бj. S. IV, 18], ‘Inspired by thee of true inspiration,’ whereby he means to say, ‘Be thou of true inspiration! go thou to Soma for us!’–‘May I obtain a support for my body, Sv─Бh─Б!’ for he who reaches the end of the sacrifice, indeed obtains a support for his body: hence he thereby means to say, ‘May I reach the end of the sacrifice!’

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon he takes out the piece of gold (from the spoon), whereby he bestows gold on men; but were he to offer (the butter) together with the gold, he would doubtless cast the gold away from men, and no gold would then be gained among men.

Eggeling
  1. He takes it out, with the text, Thou art pure, thou art shining, thou art immortal, thou art sacred to all the gods.’ When, having offered the whole milk, he now says, ‘Thou art pure . . . ,’ it is indeed pure, and shining, and immortal, and sacred to all the gods. Having loosened the grass-blade, he throws it on the barhis, and ties a string round the gold 15.

Eggeling
  1. Having then taken butter a second time in

four parts, he says, ‘Sacrificer, hold on behind 19!’ They open the (south and east) 20 doors of the hall (and walk out). On the right side (of the front door) approaches the Soma-cow 21: (by having) her thus put forward 22, he has sent her forth (to Soma); for the Soma-cow is in reality V─Бc: it is her he has gratified by this offering, thinking, ‘With her, when gratified, I will buy Soma.’

Eggeling
  1. Having gone up to her, he (the Adhvaryu) salutes her, with the text (V─Бj. S. IV, 19), ‘Thou art thought, thou art the mind,’–for speech, doubtless, speaks in accordance with thought, with the mind 24;–‘Thou art intelligence, thou art the Dakshiс╣З─Б 25,’–for it is by means of their respective intelligence 26 that people seek to make their living, either by reciting (the Veda), or by readiness of speech 27, or by songs: therefore he says, ‘Thou art intelligence;’ and ‘Dakshiс╣З─Б’ (gift to the priests) he calls her, because she is indeed the Dakshiс╣З─Б;–

‘Thou art supreme, thou art worthy of worship,’–for she is indeed supreme and worthy of worship;–‘Thou art Aditi, the double-headed,’–inasmuch as, through her (V─Бc, speech), he speaks the right thing wrongly, and puts last what comes first, and first what comes last, therefore she is double-headed: that is why he says, ‘Thou art Aditi, the double-headed 28.’

Eggeling
  1. ‘Be thou for us successful (in going) forward and successful (in coming) back!’ when he says, ‘Be thou for us successful (in going) forward,’ he means to say, ‘Go to (fetch) Soma for us!’ and when he says, ‘Be thou successful (in coming) back,’ he means to say, ‘Come back to us with Soma!’ This is why he says, ‘Be thou for us successful (in going) forward and successful (in coming) back!’

Eggeling
  1. ‘May Mitra bind thee by the foot!’ For that rope, doubtless, is of Varuс╣Зa; and were she (the cow) tied with a rope, she would be (under the power) of Varuс╣Зa. And, on the other hand, were she not tied at all, she would be uncontrolled. Now that which is of Mitra is not of Varuс╣Зa; and as (a cow), if tied with a rope, is under control, so it is in the case of this one when he says, ‘May Mitra bind thee by the foot!’

Eggeling
  1. ‘For Indra as the supreme guide;’–whereby he says, ‘May she be well-guarded!’ [He

proceeds, V─Бj. S. IV, 20], ‘May thy mother grant thee permission, thy father, thine own brother, thy fellow in the herd!’ whereby he says, ‘Go thou for us to fetch Soma, with the permission of all thy kin.’–‘O goddess, go to the god,’–for it is indeed as a goddess, as V─Бc, that she goes to a god, to Soma: therefore he says, ‘O goddess, go to the god;’–‘To Soma for the sake of Indra!’ Indra truly is the deity of the sacrifice: therefore he says, ‘To Soma for the sake of Indra.’ ‘May Rudra guide thee back!’ this he says for her safety, for cattle cannot pass beyond Rudra 31. ‘Hail to thee! come back, with Soma for thy companion!’ whereby he says, ‘Hail to thee, come back to us together with Soma!’

рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрд╕рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рдорд╛рдзрд╡реАрдпреЗ рд╡реЗрджрд╛рд░реНрдердкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдиреНрджрд┐рдиреАрдпрд╢рддрдкрдердмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рддреГрддреАрдпрдХрд╛рдгреНрдбреЗ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдердВ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН рее (рей-реи-рек)

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдбрдВ рдЧреЛрд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рдВ рдХрдирдХрд╣рдпрддреБрд▓рд╛рдкреВрд░реБрд╖реМ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдгрдЧрд░реНрднрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрд╛рдмреНрдзреАрдиреН рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╕реАрд░реАрдВрд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рджрд╢рддрд░реБрд▓рддрд╛рдзреЗрдиреБрд╕реМрд╡рд░реНрдгрднреВрдореАрдГ ред рд░рддреНрдиреЛрд╕реНрд░рд╛рдВ рд░реБрдХреНрдорд╡рд╛рдЬрд┐рджреНрд╡рд┐рдкрдорд╣рд┐рддрд░рдереМ рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрд┐рдГ рд╕рд┐рдЩреНрдЧрдгрд╛рд░реНрдпреЛ рд╡реНрдпрд╢реНрд░рд╛рдгреАрджреНрд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдЪрдХреНрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рдерд┐рддрд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рдорд╣рд╛рднреВрддрдпреБрдХреНрддрдВ рдШрдЯрдЮреНрдЪ рее реи рее

рд╢реНрд░реАрдорджреНрд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдзрд┐рд░рд╛рдЬрдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╡реИрджрд┐рдХрдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддрдХрд╢реНрд░реАрд╡реАрд░рд╣рд░рд┐рд╣рд░рдорд╣рд╛рд░рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рдореНрд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрдзреБрд░рдиреНрдзрд░реЗрдг рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпреЗрдг рд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рдорд╛рдзрд╡реАрдпреЗ рд╡реЗрджрд╛рд░реНрдердкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдиреНрджрд┐рдирд╢рддрдкрдердмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдХрд╛рдгреНрдбреЗ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпреЛ рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрдГ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее реи рее реи рее

Eggeling
  1. And as the gods then wooed her with the Gandharvas, and she turned to the gods, so does the sacrificer now woo her, and she turns to the sacrificer. They lead her (the Soma-cow) northwards round (to the place where the Soma is to be sold); for the north is the quarter of men, and hence it is that of the sacrificer for this reason they lead her northwards round.
